<span id="freeTextContainer5515420911807438038"><a href='http://psilovethatbook.blogspot.co.uk' rel='nofollow noopener'>MORE? MORE! @ P.S. I love that book!</a><br/><br/>The third and final book in Partials Sequence trilogy, oh boy oh boy I was so excited! I literary marathoned this series!<br/><br/>THE WORLD: The world gets even more interesting in this book. Besides the Island where humans live we finally get a look at the partials' everyday life and their cities. It was crazy really, very military but I loved it! And also we have war in progress with partials invading human territory and all rebels and all and just yeah wow. It is a </span>
  <span id="freeText5515420911807438038" style="display:none"><a href="http://psilovethatbook.blogspot.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">MORE? MORE! @ P.S. I love that book!</a><br /><br />The third and final book in Partials Sequence trilogy, oh boy oh boy I was so excited! I literary marathoned this series!<br /><br />THE WORLD: The world gets even more interesting in this book. Besides the Island where humans live we finally get a look at the partials' everyday life and their cities. It was crazy really, very military but I loved it! And also we have war in progress with partials invading human territory and all rebels and all and just yeah wow. It is a pretty awesome world!<br /><br /><br />CHARACTERS: Well in this book the amount of characters really improved but I will stick to the most main ones. Let's starts with Kira, I have to admit, her being all whinny was a little bit annoying and her monologues got kinda long but I still love her, she is a natural leader and a perfect female lead! Next to her there is Marcus who really grew on me since book one, he is funny and smart and very creative, he definitely made to top 3 for me from the very bottom. Marcus is a great example that Dan Wells does not just write plot based books but has also some really good character growth in them! Now, Samm...I am not sure, his parts in the beginning were a little bit boring but I guess all in all it is okay, I love how much he is devoted to Kira and well...love is love I guess. So jup, go Samm! Next, Heron. So you know how I liked her in Isolation and in Fragments she was pretty cool, well in this book she was really annoying! She just did not make any sense to me, I mean seriously. I am not saying Dan Wells wrote her wrong, I think he did a brilliant job! It is that she is a mirror of some people I know and they really make no sense to me just as her. Alright so as I mentioned there are many characters in this book so no surprise I found rather few I hate. But my mostly hated is Areal, omg she should have just died. Yeah her adopted mother tested them as children by asking them to play some activity games and noting their behavior. Yeah boohoo big deal. But no Areal hates her for that, for ruining her childhood and wants to kill the mother because you know she is EVIL. Oh please, people like Areal always tend to scream loudest even they are the most stupid. It is just like "your food is contaminated with DNA". I hate people like this so much. And on top of having Areal we also get to read about Isolde...I mean what is wrong with people, if really such people survives apocalypse then thank you but no I am not interested in saving the human race. I mean seriously, she is 17 and her biggest wish is to have a baby and how she feels the maternity instincts and all blah blah. Yeah right, I am so "believing" you, Isolde. Lack of intellect more like it. You do not get a child when you ARE a child. So annoying!<br /><br />LOVE: Kira and Samm forever :D<br /><br />PLUS: Dan Wells did a great job picturing humans. Say what you want but humans are a lost cause. Like seriously, they get off to blow up a nuclear bomb on partials and sure it will reach humans, radiations will kill the rest of them but as there is a saying or something "I can die as long as they are dead too". Just a perfect illustration of humans limitations. And also Areal and Isolde and their babies. Of that senator who wants to take a baby who is a bio weapon and kill off all partials, the baby can die for all she cares. I understand so so much why the Trust people chose Partials and not humans. This book showed so well that humans are just not worth saving.<br /><br />MINUS: What really annoyed me was Kira trying to prove how humans are equal to partials. I mean Partials have it all just like humans and plus all your senses way improved. Of course they are a superior race just like humans are superior to the monkeys. In nature, only superior races survive so it was natural that humans were gonna die out. I did not like what Kira was trying to prove, it was plainly against biology and she is supposed to be a scientist. So I think it is safe to say that no, I did not like the ending of this book.<br /><br />MINUS II: I also really did not like the whole nuclear bomb ending, I was so shocked. I mean seriously! And Armin...wasn't he supposed to be a genius? Why all geniuses are always portrayed evil? I will never understand it.<br /><br />EXTRA: I have to admit, I am so team Partials! I love the series but I hate the ending, I think it was too unrealistic.<br /><br /><a href="http://psilovethatbook.blogspot.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">MORE? MORE! @ P.S. I love that book!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5515420911807438038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18082328048600000666">Wow! This has to be in my top 5 all time favorite dystopian series ever. <br/>The battle of the partials and the humans comes to a head, people die, struggles and challenges happen. Kira is our true heroine and will it be Samm or Marcus who wins her heart? Or maybe both? Will she find her father? Will she find her purpose? Does she truly have one?   <span id="freeText18082328048600000666" style="display:none">Wow! This has to be in my top 5 all time favorite dystopian series ever. <br />The battle of the partials and the humans comes to a head, people die, struggles and challenges happen. Kira is our true heroine and will it be Samm or Marcus who wins her heart? Or maybe both? Will she find her father? Will she find her purpose? Does she truly have one? Can we all just get along?<br />The answers are coming and I won't give them away here. <br /><br />The world building was just amazing and it felt so very real to me. Isn't that what a book should do? Absolutely! That's why we read them, and what I am always searching for when I read my next book, and the next. This one stays in my head still. <br /><br />This author has a way with words, with submersing you into the world he has built and the characters themselves. I highly recommend it to people who like YA dystopian fiction. Really anyone who likes any kind of dystopian sci-fi. It is up there with the best. I want more from this author. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer7773272024164408337">You can also find this review <a href='https://bookbosomedblonde.wordpress.com/2019/04/12/book-review-ruins/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here on my blog.</a><br/><br/>A powerful and epic conclusion to a story that pushes the human race to their limit, and shows just how mighty the need to survive is, even if it goes against everything you thought you believed in.<br/><br/>The same, ever engaging writing style pulls us back into this final book and makes it hard to want to leave. The pacing was a lot slower at the beginning, following Kira’s experimentation, and Samm working with the humans to keep them alive. However, it st</span>
  <span id="freeText7773272024164408337" style="display:none">You can also find this review <a href="https://bookbosomedblonde.wordpress.com/2019/04/12/book-review-ruins/" rel="nofollow noopener">here on my blog.</a><br /><br />A powerful and epic conclusion to a story that pushes the human race to their limit, and shows just how mighty the need to survive is, even if it goes against everything you thought you believed in.<br /><br />The same, ever engaging writing style pulls us back into this final book and makes it hard to want to leave. The pacing was a lot slower at the beginning, following Kira’s experimentation, and Samm working with the humans to keep them alive. However, it still picks up rather quickly as we start to follow quite a few new points of views scattered throughout this world. I feel like because we already have been introduced to all these characters in the first two books it makes the multiple perspectives easy to go along with. and this is coming from someone who hates multiple perspectives books. That being said, we do still mostly follow Kira. and wow is she going through a lot.<br /><br />Kira is one of those characters who is ever evolving and sometimes catches us by surprise with the actions she takes. I love how she is almost portrayed in the chosen one trope, but constantly struggles to find her meaning, and we come to realise that she was never the chosen one. She is the one doing all the heavy lifting, but it was never up to her to sort out the problems that were devised before she was born, she’s just the one who makes the others realise their potential.<br /><br />Although she is one of my favourite characters, i wasn’t too keen on the love triangle type thing she was caught in. I do like that Dan explains how you can love multiple people, without meaning to but i liked when the romance was farther into the subplot in the last two books.<br /><br />The overall conclusion and the story to get there was fascinating and so complicatedly simple in the end that it made for a brilliant and mind-boggling book. I won’t be forgetting this one any time soon, and i urge you all to read this series.</span>

<div id="review_837139604" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/837139604" />
    <a title="Kinga" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4610384-kinga"><img alt="Kinga" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547289923p2/4610384.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/837139604?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kinga" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kinga" href="/user/show/4610384-kinga">Kinga</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4610384-kinga?shelf=dark-sadic">dark-sadic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4610384-kinga?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4610384-kinga?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer837139604" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7296550138592480624">Oh thanks God! Love you Dan Wells for giving us a happy ending. I'm proud of you as a reader ^^ <br/>But I'm also thorn between a 4 and a 5 star. While I loved the ending, there was so much more I would have wanted. <br/><br/>I might start off from the dedication. <br/>'This books is dedicated to everybody you hate. Sorry. Life's like that sometimes.'<br/>You threw me off. That was the truest thing I read in a long time. <br/><br/>Plot<br/>It kind of moved slowly in the beginning. For the finale of a trilogy I usually prepare myself f</span>
  <span id="freeText7296550138592480624" style="display:none">Oh thanks God! Love you Dan Wells for giving us a happy ending. I'm proud of you as a reader ^^ <br />But I'm also thorn between a 4 and a 5 star. While I loved the ending, there was so much more I would have wanted. <br /><br />I might start off from the dedication. <br />'This books is dedicated to everybody you hate. Sorry. Life's like that sometimes.'<br />You threw me off. That was the truest thing I read in a long time. <br /><br />Plot<br />It kind of moved slowly in the beginning. For the finale of a trilogy I usually prepare myself for a heart wrenching book full of battles and revelations. As the other two books it had a lot of go here and go there. I mean, half the book or even more of it is journey. There are countless of groups moving toward safety and they end up meeting through their escape. We have Samm's story, Kira, Marcus, Ariel (something I did not expect and did not like), and many more minor characters. After a few chapters I started hating the constant change of the POV. But it also gave way to a better understanding of the story.<br /><br />Kira<br />She's strong. I give you that. She's been kidnapped a few times, experimented on and she still holds herself together. I love her. Her character development was amazing. We see her growing up, from a scared teenager to a true leader. She puts her emotions away for later - I think that's because of the male author but anyway. She does her job. Eventually she realizes that she can't possibly save everyone but never gives up. She develops a few friendships, like Green(whom I loved from the beginning) but we hardly see any evolution on her 'love' side and that bugged me. It's amazing how the romance did not overcome the plot but it felt very left out. <br /><br />'Maybe you'll die and I'll end up with Samm.'<br /><br />Wouldn't I have wanted to see that? Bromance on the horizon. Marcus and Samm? Hm, it does give me a few ideas. <br /><br />Samm<br />He is my true hero. He goes from a robotic, man-made weapon and killing machine to a feeling human who's capable of love. I think he suffers the most beside Kira. They take the trophy for hardship. He is the first Partial to understand what is needed to be done to save the world. I loved seeing him struggle in the second book, trying to solve his confusing emotions that turned out to be love. He takes is upon himself the burden of saving humanity. Why? Because he trusts Kira, and he believes in her. <br /><br />'(...)you need to stop asking why people work together, and just start working together.'<br /><br />Hell yeah. And he says he's just a 'guy'. He understands that coexistence is necessary for their survival. And yes I love his definition of love:<br /><br />'Love is when you have the opportunity of turning someone's feelings or trust or vulnerability against them, but you don't. You make promises you don't want to keep, but you keep them because they are right, you help people who can't help you back.'<br /><br />In the end I think Samm is the one who symbolizes humanity the best. Not people, humanity. There's a big difference. <br /><br />Marcus<br />Well, this one made the book more enjoyable. His humor is somewhat contagious. <br /><br />'But I warn you, I will probably cry when you hurt me, and you'll feel bad about it.' <br />'Get used to it. There's a lot more useless heroics where that came from.'<br /><br />Oh but I don't think those where 'useless heroics'. Marcus as well, as our two other mains changed a lot. He became a man. He survived a rouge year. He does save a lot of them. He gives a note of lightness to all the hellish apocalypse that's lurking around them. He is capable of grand speeches when he less expects it. <br /><br />'People aren't mugs, we are clay. Living, breathing, thinking, feeling clay, and we can shape ourselves into anything we want.'<br /><br />I'm glad he had his own ending too. He was kind of pitiful in the ending if you know what I mean and I'm glad also that he did not die. Humorous people don't deserve to die. <br /><br />Minor characters<br />I have to say something because man, wasn't their presence overwhelming. We have Vale, Heron, Shon. I might have enjoyed the book more if we got to follow the main characters but here it is. Some of them were necessary. As Vale's, because he sets off the nuke. That was harsh. I did not expect it but a whole army of mad Partials wouldn't have helped Kira. Heron's Pov was interesting, because we finally get to see her emotional side. She is all about survival but in the end she understand that life, even hers, needs meaning. She learn that existing is not enough, you have to live. <br />Ariel, she, I did not like. While she does everything in her power to help her sisters she's all about killing, killing, killing Nandita. You want to do it? Fine, but don't think about it a whole book. <br /><br />Overall, I did enjoy it. Very good ending. It had closure, something that many books lack. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7296550138592480624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1558073258126237622">This book was disappointing.... It wasn't bad exactly but it had some issues...<br/><br/>First of all, I didn't like the storyline,...especially the ending! I wanted to know what happened after they made peace. Like after 10 or 20 years. I mean I thought this book was supposed to about survival, I thought it was really cool and clever from the author to actually have the two species to work together in order to survive.... and yet we see nothing of this sort at all which was disappointing and I was really</span>
  <span id="freeText1558073258126237622" style="display:none">This book was disappointing.... It wasn't bad exactly but it had some issues...<br /><br />First of all, I didn't like the storyline,...especially the ending! I wanted to know what happened after they made peace. Like after 10 or 20 years. I mean I thought this book was supposed to about survival, I thought it was really cool and clever from the author to actually have the two species to work together in order to survive.... and yet we see nothing of this sort at all which was disappointing and I was really looking forward to that... Also I liked the background story we get from the Trust but the way Armin dies was kind of predictable, a bit fast and sloppy...<br /><br />Secondly, the characters were boring... We learned nothing new about them and they didn't developed at all. I liked some of them but they were predictable and there wasn't anything really interesting about any of them... Also that "love triangle" was old and didn't add anything to the story, I thought the author tried to add some romance just to break the monotony from all the killing and running all the characters seemed to be doing in this book.... <br /> <br />Overall, this book was ok but it didn't compare at all with the other two books that I liked so much..... <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1558073258126237622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="C. S." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5769255-c-s"><img alt="C. S." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526669389p2/5769255.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1028465393?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C. S." class="user" itemprop="url" name="C. S." href="/user/show/5769255-c-s">C. S.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5769255-c-s?shelf=apocalyptic">apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1028465393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5697932386860081600">Okay... this series just got weird. Partials with gills, murderous blood-men, genetically altered creatures, changing weather patterns (no real explanation on how that happened other than some Trust guy made it his mission in life). Weird sh*t. Characters were unpredictable and the writing was monotonous. The way Kira chose the person she wanted to be with was okay, but the way Marcus reacted to it was wrong. He was way too "okay" with essentially being dumped. It was an easy way out for the aut</span>
  <span id="freeText5697932386860081600" style="display:none">Okay... this series just got weird. Partials with gills, murderous blood-men, genetically altered creatures, changing weather patterns (no real explanation on how that happened other than some Trust guy made it his mission in life). Weird sh*t. Characters were unpredictable and the writing was monotonous. The way Kira chose the person she wanted to be with was okay, but the way Marcus reacted to it was wrong. He was way too "okay" with essentially being dumped. It was an easy way out for the author that most readers won't accept. I could complain for a while, but I'll just say this was sloppily written with way too many loose ends that were never tied up. For instance, it never described how Isodole's Partial plague was actually triggered, or how or if it was turned off again. I'm just annoyed with this series right now. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5697932386860081600" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_907195695" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/907195695" />
    <a title="William" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14461220-william"><img alt="William" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458426069p2/14461220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/907195695?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="William" class="user" itemprop="url" name="William" href="/user/show/14461220-william">William</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer907195695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9481748252410529154">HOLY MOLY GUACAMOLE. Where do I even start with this series? <br/><br/>Warning to the reader: This review was written after essentially a 24-hour reading marathon with breaks for eating, bathroom, and obviously sleep. And I regret nothing of it because it was that amazing. However, if this review does not make sense, please forgive me. <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397279663ra/9258044.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Anyways... this series. Wow. <br/>First, let me start off with the world-building and let me remark on how amazing it is. <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397279663ra/9258045.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>It's basically like them ^ <br/>You expect something good an</span>
  <span id="freeText9481748252410529154" style="display:none">HOLY MOLY GUACAMOLE. Where do I even start with this series? <br><br>Warning to the reader: This review was written after essentially a 24-hour reading marathon with breaks for eating, bathroom, and obviously sleep. And I regret nothing of it because it was that amazing. However, if this review does not make sense, please forgive me. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397279663ra/9258044.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anyways... this series. Wow. <br>First, let me start off with the world-building and let me remark on how amazing it is. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397279663ra/9258045.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It's basically like them ^ <br>You expect something good and then BAM! Pure awesomeness. That basically pretty much sums up the world building. I could practically imagine all the places and people that all the characters went through and the details were so vivid that you are in the world alongside them. This is what dystopian novels are supposed to look like. The Senate &lt;3. The attempts at human civilization. UGH &lt;3. <br><br>From the world that we are introduced to, Dan Wells knows how to keep the reader engaged and on the edge of his/her seat, literally. I think my heart went through a not so healthy exercise with adrenaline just continuing to go through me at the tension, the action, and the plot twists and newfound knowledge that makes you just go like this: <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403256ra/784465.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And this: <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397279663ra/9258046.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Now, the plot. Can someone please just understand how Dan Wells just comes up with this plot? Anyone? <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397279663ra/9258047.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>No? Because the plot just blows you away in feels. Or washes you away. Whatever mood you feel like. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/548203.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>From the concept of the Partials to the Trust to the RM virus and the expiration date. I just can't. It's too good. <br><br>The characters. OMG. <br>- Kira, why are you just so perfect? Not perfect in the sense that you don't have any flaws, but the fact that you are HUMAN. You act like a human being, a relatable character that any character can relate with. Some authors fall into the trap of making their heroines too perfect. Too right. Too knowing. While some authors fall into the trap of making their characters just whiny and just plain annoying. Not Dan Wells. <br>Kira: strong, independent, sincere, an EMPATHIZER, caring, kind, and someone who also makes mistakes and isn't afraid to own up to them. THANK YOU. <br>And a feminist too, but not the judgy type <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397279663ra/9258048.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>But what I love most about her is that she STRUGGLES. She struggles with real questions and problems and works them out like any rational human being with a heart. She isn't put into the story with all of her morals set. Someone who knows what to do. She struggles with extremely difficult moral questions and she makes decisions that are uniquely her. <br><br>Side note: I am going off track because this is where I want to just express all my love for this series and why I think it is so different from every dystopian series out there and why you should give it a try. Why? Because this series asks the hard questions. <br><br>It deals with the very scary question of extinction and realistically describes and details humanity's response, both emotionally and physically. It asks the questions that we have to ask as a society and species and what our morals are. It deals and grapples with the VERY REAL issues of racism and genocide. And this series explores the rationale and thoughts between the two groups that are trying to kill each other: the Partials and humanity. The reader experiences both facets of the experience and is forced to ask themselves what is truly right. <br><br>Survival vs. Living? Can a society even have morality when it is on the brink of extinction? What are the results when we try to "play God?" Can love and understanding truly triumph over hate? Can two groups who are consumed by hate and misunderstanding ever reconcile? Is peace even possible within humanity? Are we doomed to repeat our past mistakes? <br><br>Can you kind of get why I love this series? The books in no way give a definite answer, but Kira provides the shining light that sheds a light on some of these answers and it is her vision. Her humane and HUMAN vision that makes these books beautiful. <br><br>ALL THE APPLAUSE AND LOVE. <br><br>- Marcus: How you are amazing dude. And he is one of my favorites because I kind of see a little of myself in him. &lt;3 <br>- Samm. Heron (OMG I LOVE YOU). Is there anything else to say?<br><br>All the characters. BRB CRYING. <br><br>Let me just end with one of the most powerful quotes in the book: <br><i>"If my life had no meaning, there was no reason not to end it."<br>"So you ended it?"<br>"So I gave it meaning."</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380402312ra/781883.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403256ra/784470.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397279663ra/9258049.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380402312ra/781882.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380402458ra/782282.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm done. What you should take away from this? Go read it. It's glorious and awesome and you'll thank me. Your welcome. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9481748252410529154" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+HQ9YKf3eKrMjQz0iDMiFSMsI10Figype429j6E/R81WUnBFJR2TZ5r9mJZpgT1kwZA+dA+utiuBbw9/L0xstg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('d0GUa4rG0uRgkO+SgfWJexFZjxAuRCipwWo3IJT/KfjZZ9lOCCw5KTbge/BgR5YK8+WSOSRgkis7iIXQGowCgw==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer9001561995248249418">Dan Wells is a thriller and science fiction writer. Born in Utah, he spent his early years reading and writing. He is he author of the Partials series (Partials, Isolation, Fragments, and Ruins), the John Cleaver series (I Am Not a Serial Killer, Mr. Monster, and I Don't Want To Kill You), and a few others (The Hollow City, A Night of Blacker Darkness, etc). He was a Campbell nomine for best new w</span>
  <span id="freeText9001561995248249418" style="display:none">Dan Wells is a thriller and science fiction writer. Born in Utah, he spent his early years reading and writing. He is he author of the Partials series (Partials, Isolation, Fragments, and Ruins), the John Cleaver series (I Am Not a Serial Killer, Mr. Monster, and I Don't Want To Kill You), and a few others (The Hollow City, A Night of Blacker Darkness, etc). He was a Campbell nomine for best new writer, and has won a Hugo award for his work on the podcast Writing Excuses; the podcast is also a multiple winner of the Parsec Award.</span>
